### Post by cmcanulty on 2009-09-29
I am totally frustrated  
I have no backup and no way to make one.  I have tried every mount tool and program I can find and everything fails as no permission to write, yet I set all the permissions every way I could. I've reformatted both my external drives trying to solve this and even sent one back to maker. So now I have no backup and no way to make one. It is just plain crazy that Ubuntu won't let a user write to their own devices, and insanely difficult. I have spent weeks trying to do this.Both devices work fine in windows.Currently mine shows as mounted but I can't do anything with it and even if I get a backup started it unmounts randomly and backup fails every time.Also I have a 340 GB hard drive on my laptop with about 81GB data. Yet system monitor shows a 290 disk with only 90GB free. What a mess!!! I have been trying all the directions in this web page but it is for a previous version of Ubuntu (I have 9.04) but I couldn't find a simlilar writeup for Jaunty. So some of the directions point to places that aren't on Jaunty like System->Preferences->Removable Drives and Media.here is the website link, I am really trying but this is very difficulHere is the latest error message  from grsync and yes the device shows as mounted. Currently it is Fat 32 I have also tried NTFS and ext3.rsync: recv_generator: mkdir "/media/disk/cmcanulty" failed: Input/output error (5)
*** Skipping any contents from this failed directory ***

Is their data on the hard drives already?  Are you able to view the data from within Ubuntu?

I've reformatted both my external drives trying to solve this and even sent one back to maker. So now I have no backup and no way to make one. It is just plain crazy that Ubuntu won't let a user write to their own devices, and insanely difficult. I have spent weeks trying to do this.Both devices work fine in windows.Currently mine shows as mounted but I can't do anything with it and even if I get a backup started it unmounts randomly and backup fails every time.Also I have a 340 GB hard drive on my laptop with about 81GB data. Yet system monitor shows a 290 disk with only 90GB free. What a mess!!! I have been trying all the directions in this web page but it is for a previous version of Ubuntu (I have 9.04) but I couldn't find a simlilar writeup for Jaunty. So some of the directions point to places that aren't on Jaunty like System->Preferences->Removable Drives and Media.here is the website link, I am really trying but this is very difficult [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Mount/USB](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Mount/USB)

You're always gonna have less space than the Mfgr. says, you also have to figure your swap partition and /home (if you have one).

Are your ext HDs formatted to anything other than NTFS? If it's FAT32, your backup will fail at 4 GB. Ext3 might have ownership and permission probs.

### Post by Sir Jasper on 2009-09-29
Hi,

Can you please answer a few questions:

* Is Ubuntu 9.04 your only operating system?

* Can you tell us how your 340 GB internal drive is partitioned?

* Does everything (hardware/software) work now - ie is backing-up your only problem?

* What size(s) are your external drive(s)? 

* Is there anything at all on your external drives you want/need to keep?

* What other drives do you have (Floppy, CD, DVD)?

My regards

### Post by Sir Jasper on 2009-09-29
Hi again,

In the unlikely event that you get no help with your rsync errors you might try installing ¨Simple Backup¨  available via Synaptic Package Manager.

It works for me but I only back up my home directory with Simple Backup. I clone 9.04 in its entirety 3 times a month using a paid cloning program.

If you want to try Simple Backup let us know and I will be happy to give you a few helpful hints.

My regards

### Post by samden on 2009-09-29
To use a code box you just type > [ CODE ] at the start of the text, and > [ /CODE ] at the end of it - but without any spaces  (I added spaces above so I could actually show you the text rather than it thinking I was typing code myself!).

---

### Post by Sir Jasper on 2009-09-29
Hi,

As eveything on your single internal hard drive partition is working to your satisfaction  I would suggest that howsoever that partition is formatted (ext 3, or whatever) then use that same format on your external drive that you want to backup to, unless rsync, or any other program you may use, automatically clones the original format; then there should be no need to format it at all.

My regards

---
